I hope this message finds you well. My colleagues Eric Luce (Director of Row Crops) and Ivan Wollenmann (Regional Sales Manager) have been working extensively with John Dimerly, John Buol, Steve Koziolek, Adam Baker, and Jeremiah Curry. We’ve all agreed that making CONVERGENCE BioFungicide a much larger part of the Rosen’s arsenal is a worthwhile endeavor. While reviewing our contact list, I realized that we have largely focused our outreach in Iowa, Nebraska, and Minnesota and have neglected to connect with Rosen’s personnel in other areas. With this email, I hope to begin changing that. My intentions are simple and clear. I want to bring three topics to your attention: 1. CONVERGENCE BioFungicide performance in the Midwest (2024–2025) 2. CERTIS technical training opportunities 3. DEMO product for customer trials Topic 1: CONVERGENCE BioFungicide Performance Attached is a summary of the last two years of third-party grower trials from IA, IL, NE, MN, and SD. The data suggest that farmers generally have a good opportunity for ROI with this product. In today’s market environment, there are some interesting conversations to be had around how biologicals like CONVERGENCE can complement older chemistries and help growers maintain strong disease protection without relying solely on the newest, highest-priced fungicides. Topic 2: Opportunity for CERTIS Technical Training We would like to schedule some face-to-face time for focused technical and product positioning discussions. Adam, Jeremiah, Ivan, and I are currently targeting several locations in IA and NE that strongly support Rosen’s and may value a short technical session. We would be happy to travel with you and do the same in your area as well. We have open availability over the next four weeks and could easily come to Illinois if there is interest. Topic 3: DEMO Product for Trials Third-party data from organizations like yours are extremely valuable for building regional experience. If you have DEMO product needs, feel free to reach out to me directly and I will make sure you receive what you need. If we are able to meet, we can also align on the number of trials you and your customers may want to conduct. We have both CONVERGENCE BioFungicide and LifeGard WG Plant Activator available for this season’s trials. NOTE: Ivan works with both row crops and specialty crops across the Midwest, so there may be opportunities beyond corn and soybeans that could also be worth discussing. Here are some great resources for CONVERGENCE BioFungicide: * CONVERGENCE Sell Sheet <https://www.certisbio.com/hubfs/Convergence-Sell-Sheet_07152024.pdf> * CONVERGENCE Tech Sheet <https://www.certisbio.com/hubfs/Convergence-Tech-Sheet_082224.pdf> * CONVERGENCE on Tar Spot Sheet <https://www.certisbio.com/hubfs/Convergence%20Tar%20Spot%20v15%2010.07.2024.pdf> * CONVERGENCE on Tar Spot Video <https://www.certisbio.com/blog/convergence-in-action-take-control-of-tar-spot> Here are some great resources for LifeGard WG Biological Plant Activator: * LifeGard WG Sell Sheet <https://www.certisbio.com/hubfs/LifeGard_Certis%20Sell%20Sheet.pdf> * LifeGard WG Tech Sheet <https://www.certisbio.com/hubfs/Certis%20LifeGard%20Tech%20Sheet_Beans.pdf> * LifeGard on White Mold <https://www.certisbio.com/hubfs/LifeGard_MOA_WhiteMold_071924-1.pdf> I’m very grateful for the chance to be able to work with you and hope we can connect soon – THANK YOU!"			2 Minute Read - CERTIS Introduction.msg	"Bailey, John D., PhD"	sclapp@riw2000.com' <sclapp@riw2000.com>

I’ve also adjusted my Tech Talk PPT to reflect this preference. 2024–2025 Commercial Trial Summary (n=70): CONVERGENCE used alone in Grower Standard* Crop Application Number of Trials Win Rate % Average Yield Diff. vs Grower Standard Average GROSS Revenue vs. Grower Standard** Soybean In-furrow 12 67% +1.7 bu/ac $16.61/ac Soybean Foliar 11 82% +4.6 bu/ac $47.81/ac Corn In-Furrow 29 79% +7.5 bu/ac $28.52.ac Corn Foliar 18 61% +5.1 bu/ac $12.56/ac*** *Grower Standard = The grower’s established agronomic program at each location. Programs varied by grower, geography and retailer and may or may not have included seed treatments, fertility programs, and/or foliar crop protection products. **Gross Revenue Gain = grain value of the yield difference relative to the Grower Standard. Calculated using $4.50/bu corn and $10.50/bu soybeans. ***Lower corn foliar returns in 2025 largely reflected reduced disease pressure across most trial environments. Third party data from people like you and Adam is so important to us all. I hope that you consider putting in additional trials to generate more regional data. For DEMO Product needs, reach out to me directly and I’ll see that you get it. If you have a number of trials in mind, shoot that number to me so I can get you on the list and manage our inventory. We have both CONVERGENCE and LifeGard WG being made for this season’s trials. I’m very grateful to work with you three – THANK YOU! -JDB"			2-Minute Read_  CERTIS Follow-up - Field Trials and DEMO Product.msg	"Bailey, John D., PhD"	abaker@riw2000.com' <abaker@riw2000.com>; jcurry@riw2000.com <jcurry@riw2000.com>

CONVERGENCE BioFungicide performance data in the Midwest (2024–2025) 2. CERTIS technical training opportunities 3. DEMO product for field trials Topic 1: CONVERGENCE BioFungicide Performance Attached is a summary of the last two years of third-party grower trials from IA, IL, NE, MN, and SD. The data suggest that farmers have a good opportunity for ROI with this product. Averaging over 70 third-party commercial trials, we see average responses of 5.1 bu/ac with foliar in corn, 7.5 bu/ac with in-furrow in corn, 4.6 bu/ac with foliar in soybeans, and 1.7 bu/ac with in-furrow in soybeans. In today’s market environment, there are some interesting conversations to be had around how CONVERGENCE can complement older chemistries that Rosen’s carries to help growers maintain strong disease protection without relying solely on the newest, highest-priced fungicides. Topic 2: Opportunity for CERTIS Technical Training We would like to schedule some face-to-face time for focused technical and product positioning discussions with you and select retailers of your choosing. Ivan and I are planning travel to locations in IA, NE, SD, and MN that strongly support us and value a short technical session. We would be happy to travel to you and(or) with you to your customers and provide this service. We have open availability over the next 4-6 weeks and could easily come do trainings with you. There are many, many other products that he can talk about which provides your customers with flexible opportunities beyond conventional corn and soybeans that could be worth discussing. CONVERGENCE BioFungicide performance data in the Midwest (2024–2025) 2. CERTIS technical training opportunities 3. DEMO product for field trials Topic 1: CONVERGENCE BioFungicide Performance Attached is a summary of the last two years of third-party grower trials from IA, IL, NE, MN, and SD. The data suggest that farmers have a good opportunity for ROI with this product. Averaging over 70 third-party commercial trials, we see average responses of 5.1 bu/ac with foliar in corn, 7.5 bu/ac with in-furrow in corn, 4.6 bu/ac with foliar in soybeans, and 1.7 bu/ac with in-furrow in soybeans. In today’s market environment, there are some interesting conversations to be had around how CONVERGENCE can complement older chemistries that Rosen’s carries to help growers maintain strong disease protection without relying solely on the newest, highest-priced fungicides. Programs varied by grower, geography and retailer and may or may not have included seed treatments, fertility programs, and/or foliar crop protection products. **Gross Revenue Gain = grain value of the yield difference relative to the Grower Standard. Calculated using $4.50/bu corn and $10.50/bu soybeans. ***Lower corn foliar returns in 2025 largely reflected reduced disease pressure across most trial environments. 2/13/2026	John Demerly	jdemerly@riw2000.com	Rosen's	email	introduction	5-Minute Read: Additional CONVERGENCE Data - Threshold Performance	"Hello Mr. Dimerley and Mr. Buol, I hope you all are doing well. I apologize for the delay in delivering the additional data you asked for during our MS Teams meeting on 20-JAN. Specifically, you asked me “What is your Win Rate % at 3 bu/ac?”. From the graphs below, you can see the Win Rate % at ? 3 bu/ac = 55% for in-furrow in corn, 43% for foliar in corn, 25% for soybeans in-furrow, and 45% for soybeans foliar. These threshold response curves for the 70 commercial trials isolate CONVERGENCE’s intrinsic biological value without tank-mix partners. In this context, in-furrow placement anchors consistency and ROI efficiency, especially in corn, while foliar placement concentrates upside yield potential—most clearly in soybeans but also quite consistently in corn. This reinforces CONVERGENCE’s strongest commercial fit as a program-building biological: stabilizing outcomes in-furrow and unlocking upside through foliar integration with or without chemistry, depending on in-season conditions. For your convenience, I also include here the ROI table from our previous discussion. CONVERGENCE Bio-Fungicide ROI Efficiency: Crop Application Number of Trials Average Net Rev Gain* Overall Win Rate (%) Win Rate at 2:1 ROI** Win Rate at 3:1 ROI** Corn In-Furrow 29 $28.52 79% 52% 45% Corn Foliar 18 $12.56 68% 28% 28% Soybean In-Furrow 12 $16.61 67% 42% 25% Soybean Foliar 11 $47.81 82% 45% 36% *NET Revenue Gain reflects value after product cost and uses an average MSRP of $82.00/gallon, 8 fl oz/ac in-furrow, 16 fl oz/ac foliar), $4.50 corn and $10.50 soybeans. **Win rates at 2:1 and 3:1 ROI are tiered thresholds (i.e., 3:1 outcomes are a subset of 2:1 outcomes). I trust this answers your question directly. Feel free to reach out for further discussion. Best Regards, -JDB"			5-Minute Read_  Additional CONVERGENCE Data - Threshold Performance.msg	"Bailey, John D., PhD"	John Demerly (jdemerly@riw2000.com) <jdemerly@riw2000.com>

Key Point 3: 2026 Field Trial Programs We’re actively planning the 2026 Commercial Field Trial program and would value your input on priority crops, geographies, and use-cases. Demo product and technical expertise will be available to support your field trial programs. Let’s nail this down during our meeting. 4/14/2026	Luke Gosse	lukejgosse@gmail.com		email	evaluation	CERTIS Follow-up - Field Maps and DEMO Trials	"Sir Luke, Thanks for the map and the notes on how each field is farmed — that helped tighten this up so it fits with your operation. I created a crude drawing and attached it for clarity (not to scale). I then tried to align the layouts with your directions: * Field north of 270th Street ? farmed North to South * Field south of 270th Street ? farmed East to West Field North of 270th Street (~148 ac) Farming direction: North ? South (N–S passes) We can use a block-style layout, running with your normal N–S passes. I thought Iwe could keep the two smaller triangle areas as untreated checks (UTCs), so we’re not forcing awkward math in there. Layout moving West ? East across the field: * UTCs (NW and SE triangle areas, ~36 acres) * Block 1: 16 acres - LifeGard® WG Early – Spray first pass up to V4-V5 with herbicide (16 ac load = 1 packet) * Block 2: 40 acres - CONVERGENCE® BioFungicide Late – Spray Late at VT-R1 (40 ac load = 1 case) with drone * Block 3: 16 acres - LifeGard® WG Late – Spray Late at VT-R1 (16 ac load = 1 packet) with drone * Block 4: 40 acres - CONVERGENCE® BioFungicide Early – Spray first pass up to V4-V5 with herbicide (40 ac load = 1 case) Why this works well: * Those two triangular areas naturally stay untreated and serve as your UTCs * No need to spray around them or force straight edges * All main treatments run clean with your N–S farming pattern * This field gives us large-scale, real-world performance comparisons Field South of 270th Street (~104 ac) Farming direction: East ? West (E–W passes) We can use a strip trial layout for this field, aligned with your E–W passes so everything flows naturally. Layout (North ? South across the field): 1. Strip 1: ~18 acres - UTC (north strip, ~18 acres) 2. Strip 2: 16 ac - LifeGard® WG Early – Spray first pass up to V4-V5 with herbicide (16 ac load = 1 packet) 3. Strip 3: 16 ac - LifeGard® WG Late – Spray Late at VT-R1 (16 ac load = 1 packet) with drone 4. Strip 4: 20 acres - CONVERGENCE® BioFungicide Early – Spray first pass up to V4-V5 with herbicide (20 ac load = 1, 2.5-gal jug) 5. Strip 5: 20 acres - CONVERGENCE® BioFungicide Late – Spray Late at VT-R1 (20 ac load = 1, 2.5-gal jug) with drone 6. Strip 6: ~16–20 ac UTC (south strip) Why this works well: * LifeGard® WG: 1 packet = 16 acres ? each strip = exactly 1 packet * CONVERGENCE® BioFungicide: 2.5 gal jug treats 20 acres ? each strip = exactly 1 jug * Everything lines up clean — no partials, no guesswork in the tank * This field gives us side-by-side comparisons within the same environment What I hope we get out of this: Even without replicates, these layouts will let us look at: * Product comparison (LifeGard® WG vs CONVERGENCE® BioFungicide) * Timing comparison (Early vs Late) * Field-scale performance (north field) * Side-by-side strip differences (south field) Hopefully, it doesn’t slow you down or disrupting your normal workflow. If this looks good, let me know and I can put together a simple one-page spray protocol for the cab, so everything is easy to follow when you’re spraying. Appreciate you working through this — I think this will give us some useful insight this season. Thanks, John"			CERTIS Follow-up - Field Maps and DEMO Trials.msg	"Bailey, John D., PhD"	Luke Gosse <lukejgosse@gmail.com>

3/13/2026	Matthew J. Oswald	moswald@cpicoop.com	Cooperative Producers Inc.	email	technical_training	#NAME?	"Thanks Matt. I’ll send it over ASAP. I assume it’s all corn. You can have a look in the document at the additional data that one might want to take. It’s not that we need the data on our end – of course, I’m a data guy, so, I like to get it but, basically, do whatever you think will help your agronomists sell the product in the future. For in-furrow application, a stand count at V4-V6 can be useful – I also like to do early disease incidence/severity ratings at this point. If one can follow-up with late-season disease assessments, that usually helps us separate trials where products “don’t work” because of a lack of disease pressure. If we don’t have any idea of disease pressure and there’s no difference in yield, we don’t know if the product just failed OR the yield limited factor that the technology addresses just wasn’t there. Farmer trials are often like that – you and farmers (and me) have limited time as a resource to go and do assessments on large scale. I’ll try to help you if I can. One thing to make sure you and I align on is expectations. In-furrow applications of CONVERGENCE are going to help with pythium spp., phytopthera spp., rhizoctonia spp., etc. – so, soil-bourne seedling diseases. We also claim suppression of nematodes on the label (that’s probably a bigger deal than most people realize). Point is, If tar spot or rust comes in later, this treatment will not touch any of those leaf diseases – one would have to make an additional applications to protect the crop against yield loss. So, quick CONVERGENCE math to make sure I get you the right amount = 3 trials x 40 acresCONVERGENCE/trial = 120 acres x 8 fl oz/acre = 7.5 gallons needed (1.5 cases of 2x2.5s). Look right to you? Best Regards, John D. 4/1/2026	Stephen Eschenbach	seschenbach@newcoop.com	NEW Cooperative	email	technical_training	"Eric@CERTIS: Intro of Stephen Eschenbach, NEW Coop. to John Bailey and Ivan Wollenmann CERTIS Biologicals"	"Hi Stephen, Really appreciate the quick response — sounds like you’ve got a solid plan in mind. Rather than get too deep into trial design over email, I think it would be best for us to connect face-to-face next week. Ivan is traveling here to Iowa and it’s a good opportunity to connect. If so, we can briefly review the tech side, walk through use patterns, and align on objectives. Setting things up to generate the most meaningful data for you and your customers is a top priority. That said, just a couple quick thoughts to answer your questions directly: Foliar Timing for Leaf Disease Focus: Most of the results I sent you are from adding CONVERGENCE® on top of a Grower Standard Program (sometimes, that included a chemical fungicide and sometimes it didn’t) at that VT/R1 timing in corn and R2/R3 in soybeans. These tend to line up well with typical 2nd pass programs which normally are meant to protect that upper canopy during peak disease pressure. There’s certainly a place for earlier foliar applications, but strategically, what the market is telling us is that growers are looking for a more cost-effective second-pass option compared to the newer chemistries that carry a pretty hefty price tag. Given current market conditions, either as a standalone or tank-mixed with a cost-effective generic, CONVERGENCE® BioFungicide tends to fit really well in that context. Recommended Rates: * Foliar: 16 fl oz/ac * In-Furrow: 8 fl oz/ac Note: Each of us on the Row Crop team have been working with biologicals for at least 20 years. We tend to agree that for Bacillus based biofungicides like CONVERGENCE®, it usually does not follow that increasing the rate increases the effect. On the contrary – a lot of times, “less is more”. Trial Approach: I am sure you’ve ran plenty of trials and have a good handle on what works — your approach with multiple locations and hybrid/variety selection makes a lot of sense. From my experiences with split-field trials, I try to emphasize making sure there’s a clear baseline/control to measure against on both sides of the field. This can be difficult to achieve, but data that tells a clean story are often more useful regardless of how the trials are ultimately structured. We’ve got DEMO product available and can support however you want to set these up — we can sort through locations, quantities, and logistics when we meet. Looking forward to connecting around your schedule. Best Regards, John D.
